    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer1884220349527504579">Larry is a teenager wrestling not only with his sexuality and the implications of a physical relationship with his younger brother, but with the very point of his existence. He is numb to almost all that surrounds him. As the book opens, Larry has been paid $500 by a senior to kill a fellow student and retrieve the boy's notebook. It seems simple enough. However, once Larr</span>
  <span id="freeText1884220349527504579" style="display:none">Larry is a teenager wrestling not only with his sexuality and the implications of a physical relationship with his younger brother, but with the very point of his existence. He is numb to almost all that surrounds him. As the book opens, Larry has been paid $500 by a senior to kill a fellow student and retrieve the boy's notebook. It seems simple enough. However, once Larry delves into the notebook, complications arise. An immensely powerful work that explores teenage depression, moral vacuity, and the confusion of love, this is a claustrophobic and harrowing piece of fiction.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12686060201668631673">This was my first experience with Dennis Cooper and wow it was a wild ride. A guy at a bookstore I frequent told me to check him and out and he was not wrong. This story is outrageous and weird but also incredibly good. This novel is all over the place. Cooper really puts you in the head of the protagonist and he can’t make sense of anything. It made it hard for me to sometimes understand what was happening. I had to reread the same passage a couple times throughout this book. Be prepared for al</span>
  <span id="freeText12686060201668631673" style="display:none">This was my first experience with Dennis Cooper and wow it was a wild ride. A guy at a bookstore I frequent told me to check him and out and he was not wrong. This story is outrageous and weird but also incredibly good. This novel is all over the place. Cooper really puts you in the head of the protagonist and he can’t make sense of anything. It made it hard for me to sometimes understand what was happening. I had to reread the same passage a couple times throughout this book. Be prepared for all the trigger warnings with this one, but I say give it a shot!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12686060201668631673" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16812778525832323295">One of Dennis Cooper's most incredible works. Two gay brothers (one who accepts what he is, the other denies it) both fall in love with the same boy - a depressed teenager with no real capacity for love. The boys' rejection sends them into the arms of one another, fulfilling the sexual/physical desires they imagine having with their disturbed friend. The teen kills himself, which sends the brothers into confusion and insanity. Unbelievably sad, scary, and painful. Cooper is brutally honest in hi</span>
  <span id="freeText16812778525832323295" style="display:none">One of Dennis Cooper's most incredible works. Two gay brothers (one who accepts what he is, the other denies it) both fall in love with the same boy - a depressed teenager with no real capacity for love. The boys' rejection sends them into the arms of one another, fulfilling the sexual/physical desires they imagine having with their disturbed friend. The teen kills himself, which sends the brothers into confusion and insanity. Unbelievably sad, scary, and painful. Cooper is brutally honest in his depiction of gay teenage life, desire, and rejection - and all the psychological turmoil that can ensue. Cooper is a contemporary William S. Burroughs, holding back nothing - giving more than is perhaps consumable.. </span>

<div id="review_1529160892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1529160892" />
    <a title="Nate D" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/406701-nate-d"><img alt="Nate D" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1203897989p2/406701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1529160892?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nate D" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nate D" href="/user/show/406701-nate-d">Nate D</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781841952741" href="/book/show/2025865.My_Loose_Thread">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406701-nate-d?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/406701-nate-d?shelf=new-narrative">new-narrative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1529160892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1673777511781404131">Despite the extreme emotions (actually extreme numbness mixed with emotions), and continual extremes of plot movement and backstory, this is actually sort of straight-forward for Dennis Cooper. He includes a notebook within the story which you might expect to modify the reader's certainty of whose narrative they're actually reading, but that never really happens. Instead this all feels strangely unconceptual and direct. Any confusion here isn't generally structural or philosophic so much as just</span>
  <span id="freeText1673777511781404131" style="display:none">Despite the extreme emotions (actually extreme numbness mixed with emotions), and continual extremes of plot movement and backstory, this is actually sort of straight-forward for Dennis Cooper. He includes a notebook within the story which you might expect to modify the reader's certainty of whose narrative they're actually reading, but that never really happens. Instead this all feels strangely unconceptual and direct. Any confusion here isn't generally structural or philosophic so much as just the muddled sensations of teen years (taken to notable extremes). I dunno, that's all well and good, but without more theoretical aparatuses in place, this reads more like a catalogue of dissociated disturbing actions, more like Less Than Zero than The Notebook, The Proof, and The third Lie, say. AND it seems to be written at least in part in response to one of the media hot button topics of its era, one which I've only really seen addresses effectively when way more oblique than this.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_304843889" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304843889" />
    <a title="Rupert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/121599-rupert"><img alt="Rupert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442476378p2/121599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304843889?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rupert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rupert" href="/user/show/121599-rupert">Rupert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304843889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14275931140508243500">In My Loose Thread, Dennis Cooper peers through the eyes of a teen psychotic to paint a convincing portrait of contemporary high school as a limbo of repressed and confused sexuality, inhabited by teens experiencing various gray shades of depression and blood/drug/alcohol toxicity levels. It's not a novel to sit down and savor, but one that yanks you in, perhaps against your wishes. By the end, you no longer wonder how tragedies like Columbine happen, but why they don't happen more often.<br/><br/>The dis</span>
  <span id="freeText14275931140508243500" style="display:none">In My Loose Thread, Dennis Cooper peers through the eyes of a teen psychotic to paint a convincing portrait of contemporary high school as a limbo of repressed and confused sexuality, inhabited by teens experiencing various gray shades of depression and blood/drug/alcohol toxicity levels. It's not a novel to sit down and savor, but one that yanks you in, perhaps against your wishes. By the end, you no longer wonder how tragedies like Columbine happen, but why they don't happen more often.<br /><br />The dissociating narrator of this disturbing tale is a convincing psychotic named Larry whose dad has debilitating cancer and whose mom is an alcoholic. Larry fears that he might be gay, and lashes out violently in moments of uncomfortable sexual ambiguity: "I just hit Pete, not that hard. It was either hit him, or turn gay. I think I was gay for a minute."<br /><br />Larry has been sleeping with his brother Jim (but it's Jim who's gay, not him, Larry thinks); meanwhile, he has been hired by the school nazi, Gilman, to kill Bill, Jim's best friend. Gilman seems to draw people to him simply because his beliefs remain fairly constant, even if they are rancid. In an emotionally harrowing scene, a physically scarred, martyrlike Bill makes an impression on Larry with his honesty, both in person and in the journal notebook he's written, which Gilman wants destroyed. But Larry decides the notebook contains truth and that it should be burned because truth is what he and all his friends are most afraid of.<br /><br />Cooper's novel reads a bit like a macabre after-school-special enactment of Wilhelm Reich's The Mass Psychology of Fascism, narrated in a flat free-verse style by a trailer park Holden Caulfield with serious rage issues. But My Loose Thread depicts an all-too-believable battlefield of teen insecurity where the characters' fear of their own sexuality and lack of ability to express affection drives them to grotesque acts of violence against innocent others: If they strike first, then maybe no one will find their soft underbelly.<br /><br /> <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14275931140508243500" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3741107539890434353">One has to wonder if teenage protagonists and a teenage narrator dealing with teenage problems automatically make a book "YA". Of course, I didn't hear back from her.</span>

The plot was underdeveloped, the characters even more so, it just didn't go anywhere. "I'm not gay" was basically the plot. Loved a lot of his other works but this was awful. Sorry, Coops.</span>

<div id="review_103288650" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103288650" />
    <a title="Sean Meriwether" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3748306-sean-meriwether"><img alt="Sean Meriwether" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479315249p2/3748306.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103288650?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Meriwether" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Meriwether" href="/user/show/3748306-sean-meriwether">Sean Meriwether</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3748306-sean-meriwether?shelf=lgtbq">lgtbq</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103288650" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16169386125074296329">Dennis Cooper my well be the David Lynch of queer culture. His shockaholic fiction ignores the superficial and drives straight down the dark road of teenaged boys emotionally ruined by the fragmented environments they inhabit. "My Loose Thread" is no exception, and is a tight and destructive addition to his marganalized opus. The novel centers on Larry, a boy who has so little control over his own life and sexual drives that he numbly repeats, "I'm really confused" like a modern-day mantra. He's</span>
  <span id="freeText16169386125074296329" style="display:none">Dennis Cooper my well be the David Lynch of queer culture. His shockaholic fiction ignores the superficial and drives straight down the dark road of teenaged boys emotionally ruined by the fragmented environments they inhabit. "My Loose Thread" is no exception, and is a tight and destructive addition to his marganalized opus. The novel centers on Larry, a boy who has so little control over his own life and sexual drives that he numbly repeats, "I'm really confused" like a modern-day mantra. He's got a lot of baggage, with an accidental slaying of a boy who loved him, a sexually abusive relationship with his 13 year-old brother, and an overpowering rage when he fucks other men. He's not gay, he claims, and he's not alone--Larry's world is overflowing with guys who aren't gay, but turn their sex into violence like off-screen heroes, the boys from Columbine who killed fellow students in a secret pact because they couldn't have sex. This is a study in dysfunctional American "culture" that worships violence over intimacy. As graphic as the alluded to sex and violence becomes, Cooper maintains a clinical distance that forces you into a submissive voyeuristic position. Share his nihlistic vision, if you dare!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16169386125074296329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2624018135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7405292539516793643">This book SUCKS! This is easily one of the WORST books I've read in a long time which is a bummer because I've been meaning to read this fkn guy for a while, but, good Lord, this book was so underwhelming.<br/><br/>Hey, Dennis Cooper fans, is he always this bad? I'll probably still give Closer a shot, but my expectations have been absolutely decimated and that book has since plummeted to the bottom of my to-read list.<br/><br/>I see this dude mentioned by the same circles that frik with Guyotat, Genet, Sotos, de Sa</span>
  <span id="freeText7405292539516793643" style="display:none">This book SUCKS! This is easily one of the WORST books I've read in a long time which is a bummer because I've been meaning to read this fkn guy for a while, but, good Lord, this book was so underwhelming.<br /><br />Hey, Dennis Cooper fans, is he always this bad? I'll probably still give Closer a shot, but my expectations have been absolutely decimated and that book has since plummeted to the bottom of my to-read list.<br /><br />I see this dude mentioned by the same circles that frik with Guyotat, Genet, Sotos, de Sade, Mishima - all those weirdos - so I had high hopes for this book, but, man, the characters in this book are so flat, and the writing was just awful that I couldn't enjoy it at all.<br /><br />The story seems interesting enough on its own - a neglected child struggling with questions of his own sexuality, his murder of an ex-friend, and his sexual relationship with his 13 year-old brother has been hired to kill another student and destroy his journal - but nothing is explored with any sort of depth or attention. For a story dealing with certain sexual issues, one would like assume there to be some sort of, ahem, deeper penetration into them, but no attempt at exactitude or even the most cursory analysis/investigation into certain characters' thoughts or motives is seen.<br /><br />For example, we merely know his mother's an alcoholic because she appears twice in the book, once when incapacitated and unconscious on his return home, and another during an underwhelming scene following his attempted murder of his brother. The ending, too, was so comically underwhelming. It was a school shooting that comes out of nowhere. I started laughing once I finished the book the way a bully laughs at the kid they pick on when he does something stupid. I didn't have a damn clue why it happened or what the killer's motivation was. Everything just kind of happens in this book for it's own sake.<br /><br />This book was so shallow and sparse and boring. I felt like I was reading some edgy young adult novel due to how sophomoric and plain the prose was. But I've prattled on enough. Basically, the book sucks. Alright...see ya.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7405292539516793643" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3235703465" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3235703465" />
    <a title="Paul" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/89241745-paul"><img alt="Paul" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542105109p2/89241745.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3235703465?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/89241745-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3235703465" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8721886101619547870">I'm not exactly sure why I picked up <b>My Loose Thread</b> by <i>Dennis Cooper</i> but I'm uncomfortably glad that I did. I have to admit that I found the initial few pages a bit hard to grasp but, due to it being a fairly short novella, I plugged away at it and found a picture that built before me. A hideous, broken, grim picture of awful teenage angst and mental issues. After I finished I went back and re-read those first few pages I'd struggled through and they all made sense. Maybe I just couldn't tune i</span>
  <span id="freeText8721886101619547870" style="display:none">I'm not exactly sure why I picked up <b>My Loose Thread</b> by <i>Dennis Cooper</i> but I'm uncomfortably glad that I did. I have to admit that I found the initial few pages a bit hard to grasp but, due to it being a fairly short novella, I plugged away at it and found a picture that built before me. A hideous, broken, grim picture of awful teenage angst and mental issues. After I finished I went back and re-read those first few pages I'd struggled through and they all made sense. Maybe I just couldn't tune into the style, perhaps I'd come off the back of a book that was verbose and overwhelmingly happy to hit you over the head with information (Tropic of Capricorn), and maybe I just needed to bed down into the fractured, frustrating world the story takes place in. I'll try not to spoil anything but it's written from the point of view of Larry, a messed up kid with a messed up brother with a mother who is a lush and a father who seems to exists in body only. He did something or he thinks he did (he can't tell what's going on anymore) and he believes it's sent him spiraling out of control. It never lets up. It's dirty and confusing and surly and a mess of teenagers who can't deal with their emotions at the best of times and these are definitely not the best of times. Morbid from the very get-go the story branches off into far more twisted lands but because Larry is so disconnected it's up to us to fill in blanks.<br />It's an interesting read and exists in a period of time in recent American history where black trench-coats and disenchantment and the flavour of day. I suppose we shouldn't be so stupid as to consider this sort of tale as being from a different time as it could happen again, and probably will, but it does feel like a period piece reading it in 2020. <br />If you like something weird and bleak you'll dig this but if you don't then I can't suggest it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8721886101619547870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

You don’t quite grasp the implications as the bullet fires, but then almost as soon as it’s started this short read is over, and the ringing stops, and all that’s left is to survey the damage.</span>

<div id="review_1248735443" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1248735443" />
    <a title="kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33906101-kim"><img alt="kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1428450806p2/33906101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1248735443?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="kim" href="/user/show/33906101-kim">kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/16085775-my-loose-thread">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33906101-kim?shelf=post-modern-lit">post-modern-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33906101-kim?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33906101-kim?shelf=lgbt-fiction">lgbt-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1248735443" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1302527894308741894">First of all, what you should always remember is that Larry, the protagonist, is the most unreliable of unreliable narrators and knowing that will save you a lot of confusion. <br/><br/>It starts in media res, or maybe just after all the most important things happened. The prose isn't much to comment on. In fact it's simpler than simple. But that's the point. If you were to remove one word the whole thing would fall apart into incoherence. There are no million dollar words or saturated descriptions.<br/><br/>In fac</span>
  <span id="freeText1302527894308741894" style="display:none">First of all, what you should always remember is that Larry, the protagonist, is the most unreliable of unreliable narrators and knowing that will save you a lot of confusion. <br /><br />It starts in media res, or maybe just after all the most important things happened. The prose isn't much to comment on. In fact it's simpler than simple. But that's the point. If you were to remove one word the whole thing would fall apart into incoherence. There are no million dollar words or saturated descriptions.<br /><br />In fact, in the beginning, I felt there weren't enough of them. I was confused and thrown off. The material was hazy at best, like wool fibers not yet spooled. Eventually you make a cardigan out of it (heh) and just when you think it's enough to keep you warm, it begins to fray. You're left with one loose thread. What the protagonist does with it is left open ended.<br /><br />I should say this because it would help many of you stick with the story. Larry's psychiatrist tells Larry he spends too much time blaming himself for things that he's not guilty of, and deferring responsibility for things he <i>has</i> done.<br /><br />One more thing about Larry you should know is he's incredibly narcissistic not because he believes he's better than anyone, in fact it's the opposite, but because he believes everyone's lives revolve around him. <br /><br />If you're expecting some huge climatic scene where Larry experiences some sort of cathartic self-revelation, you'll be sorely disappointed and annoyed. It's a bit more subtle than that. The truth eventually comes together.<br /><br />In spite of all this, or maybe because of it, I enjoyed it. I was able to empathize with Larry although I disliked him and his unintentional passivity. Is it edgy? Ummm, not really unless you think of the subject matter (crisis over sexuality, gay incest, murder, and suicide) is. If you watch Investigative Discovery as obsessively as I do than it is rather tame compared to what real people do to real persons. <br /><br />If you're afraid of gore or explicit sex, then you have NOTHING to worry about.<br /><br />Give the book a chance. You might like it. I did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1302527894308741894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_192055409" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/192055409" />
    <a title="Johanna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5265134-johanna"><img alt="Johanna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567683338p2/5265134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/192055409?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johanna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johanna" href="/user/show/5265134-johanna">Johanna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer192055409" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10630815146590160424">There was nothing terribly positive about this story; in fact, I didn’t find anything that redeemed the appalling subject matter in the writing. The story is based around Larry who routinely admits to being confused by his actions and the actions of those around him. The novel tackles subject matter such as incest, murder, self-harm, school shootings, and homosexuality versus homophobia – all in all it was not a pleasant read. I felt like the novelist was using Larry’s confusion as an excuse for</span>
  <span id="freeText10630815146590160424" style="display:none">There was nothing terribly positive about this story; in fact, I didn’t find anything that redeemed the appalling subject matter in the writing. The story is based around Larry who routinely admits to being confused by his actions and the actions of those around him. The novel tackles subject matter such as incest, murder, self-harm, school shootings, and homosexuality versus homophobia – all in all it was not a pleasant read. I felt like the novelist was using Larry’s confusion as an excuse for his behaviour towards his brother, his family, and his schoolmates, when there was no legitimate reason for the amount of violence displayed by the protagonist. The style of prose was not particularly impressive, nor did it illuminate the plot very well. I’m not sure if the writer was aiming for a detached style of writing, or honestly had little idea of the subject matter he was handling, but it did not compliment the story or help create reader identification with any of the characters. I find that what people class to be ‘good writing’ usually falls into two categories: the first is that the writer has skilfully used prose to create an enthralling story, and the second in which the subject matter is so shocking and so far removed from conventional writing that it is often classed as ‘ingenious’ or ‘brave’ storytelling. This novel falls into the second category.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10630815146590160424" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6583965732078283995" style="display:none">This book pissed me off. The cover is filled with accolades about the writer. They say only <i>he</i> can tackle such a dangerous subject and get away with it. Bullshit. He shouldn't have got away with it.<br /><br />The story is about a bunch of idiot teens that are obsessed with gayness, sex, murder, and self-punishment. Many of them are <i>cutters</i> and wear the body scars like war medals. Obviously inspired by all of the recent school shooting and in particular the Columbine incident, the book follows one idiot as he tries to learn why he's so fucked up. Written in the first person point-of-view by a kid who can't even think one coherent thought it rambles on in disjointed sentences and clunky thoughts.<br /><br />If shooting, hacking up, and strangling your school mates is not enough, Dennis threw in a little incestuous sex and gay issues along with a juvenile Nazi fan club.<br /><br />It's just a stupid book. I gave it two stars because it was short and I liked the shrink who was an even bigger idiot.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1179373449" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1179373449?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matthew" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matthew" href="/user/show/128787-matthew">Matthew</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1179373449" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13745340230584866328">This is one of the sickest stories I've read. That's not why I gave it 2 stars though. I've read some sick shit before. Hello, I love Stephen King! However the author of this novel, compared by some critics as a modern day Burroughs, makes his material hard to read. It's disjointed not only in prose but in story-line. Perhaps this was done purposely as the teens (and adults) in the novel are completely out of tune. Every character in this short book, with the possible exception of Larry's younge</span>
  <span id="freeText13745340230584866328" style="display:none">This is one of the sickest stories I've read. That's not why I gave it 2 stars though. I've read some sick shit before. Hello, I love Stephen King! However the author of this novel, compared by some critics as a modern day Burroughs, makes his material hard to read. It's disjointed not only in prose but in story-line. Perhaps this was done purposely as the teens (and adults) in the novel are completely out of tune. Every character in this short book, with the possible exception of Larry's younger brother, Jim, is way off the path. For the most part, not in a "good read" way either. I got some of the reasons why Larry and his "friends" did the horrific things they did, yet others seemed out of place. There was a story to be told here. I'll give it 2 stars for that. Yet if you want to read and re-read what happens to many teenagers that are just fucked up, give it a shot. I'll give this author another chance. I just hope next time it's worth my while. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13745340230584866328" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lauren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10531362-lauren"><img alt="Lauren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340830501p2/10531362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/356924603?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/10531362-lauren">Lauren</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer356924603" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12157607531509474918">This was definitely not the book I was expecting when a friend of mine tossed it into a Christmas package alongside a hand-knitted scarf and sugar cookies. From the beginning to the end, I felt so sure that at some point, things were going to start looking up for someone, anyone in the story...but that was wishful thinking on a very grand scale. The dark, gritty subject matter was only bearable for me through the lens of the almost completely detached style it was written in. While reading I fel</span>
  <span id="freeText12157607531509474918" style="display:none">This was definitely not the book I was expecting when a friend of mine tossed it into a Christmas package alongside a hand-knitted scarf and sugar cookies. From the beginning to the end, I felt so sure that at some point, things were going to start looking up for someone, anyone in the story...but that was wishful thinking on a very grand scale. The dark, gritty subject matter was only bearable for me through the lens of the almost completely detached style it was written in. While reading I felt pulled to finish (and in fact did read the entire book in one sitting for that reason), but after putting down the book I felt disappointed as well as confused. Maybe it's Cooper's style that is throwing me off; I feel like I might have enjoyed the themes and emotions threaded through this much more if I felt I had more reason to care about the characters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12157607531509474918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DidURGOZGQN+0jqzMzhT3XL4KWXloKmyuqdMporLHrvPoSwyoE2eeUuLK1bzClVDUKqg1i9Mtr7SPUJmTuB4ww==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_436806'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/436806.Story_of_the_Eye?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Story of the Eye<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/20842.Georges_Bataille?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Georges Bataille<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.66 avg rating &mdash; 16,541 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1928\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer2868007840579662697\">Only Georges Bataille could write, of an eyeball removed from a corpse, that \"the caress of the eye over the skin is so utterly, so extraordinarily gentle, and the sensation is so bizarre that it has something of a rooster\'s horrible crowing.\" Batail<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2868007840579662697\" style=\"display:none\">Only Georges Bataille could write, of an eyeball removed from a corpse, that &quot;the caress of the eye over the skin is so utterly, so extraordinarily gentle, and the sensation is so bizarre that it has something of a rooster\'s horrible crowing.&quot; Bataille has been called a &quot;metaphysician of evil,&quot; specializing in blasphemy, profanation, and horror.\n\nStory of the Eye, written in 1928, is his best-known work; it is unashamedly surrealistic, both disgusting and fascinating, and packed with seemingly endless violations. Burroughs<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.59 avg rating &mdash; 11,931 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1985\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer4568542316523940015\">Escrita en 1952 pero no publicada hasta 1985 debido a su franca plasmación del deseo homosexual, \"Queer\", obra temprana de William S. Burroughs, es al mismo tiempo un descarnado autorretrato narrativo, una historia de amor brutalmente realista, una g<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4568542316523940015\" style=\"display:none\">Escrita en 1952 pero no publicada hasta 1985 debido a su franca plasmación del deseo homosexual, &quot;Queer&quot;, obra temprana de William S. Burroughs, es al mismo tiempo un descarnado autorretrato narrativo, una historia de amor brutalmente realista, una grotesca fantasía tragicómica y una ingeniosa novela política. Un libro que proporciona muchas claves fundamentales para adentrarse en el arrollador universo literario del autor. Esta edición definitiva, editada con motivo del 25 aniversario de su primera publicación, incorpora una extensa y documentada introducción de Oliver Harris en la que se repasan las complejas circunstancias personales en las que la obra fue escrita y que marcarían la vida y la posterior trayectoria literaria de Burroughs. Y se incluye también, a modo de epílogo, el texto que el propio autor escribió como prólogo para la edición de 1985.\n\n&quot;Queer&quot; está ambientada en un inmenso suburbio, que Burroughs definiría más tarde como la «Interzona», y que abarca desde la Ciudad de México, capital mundial del delito, hasta Panamá. Un álter ego del escritor, Lee, teje su tela amorosa en torno a Allerton, un joven ambiguo, indiferente como un animal. Deambula por locales cada vez más sórdidos, en los que pulula una fauna en estado de descomposición, y en esas excursiones, como un pícaro alienado, nos regala astillas radiactivas de su negrísimo humor. Para resolver sus obsesiones mortíferas y sexuales, Lee parte con su amigo a la búsqueda de la ayahuasca, droga absoluta capaz de otorgar el control total sobre los cerebros, y por eso mismo codiciada por Rusia y Estados Unidos... y por todo adicto. Dispuesto a abismarse en todos los peligros, como un santo o un criminal con orden de búsqueda y captura, Lee no tiene nada que perder. En esta novela aflora por primera vez ese paisaje alucinado que hoy todo lector reconoce como el mundo particular de William S. It’s the tale of a runaway that assumed the title of Countess and then went on to fool the FBI, DEA, and Interpol—as well as a number of other celebrities and institutions—with an elaborate tale of world intrigue.\n\nA NOTE FROM THE AUTHOR: Hello everyone. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer828811845439897156">Dennis Cooper was born on January 10, 1953 and grew up in the Southern California cities of Covina and Arcadia. In 1976, he founded Little Caesar Magazine and Press, which he ran until 1982. In 1985, he moved to Amsterdam for two and a half years, where he began his ten year long project, The George Miles Cycle, an interconnected sequence of five novels that includes Closer, Frisk, Try, Guide, and</span>
  <span id="freeText828811845439897156" style="display:none">Dennis Cooper was born on January 10, 1953 and grew up in the Southern California cities of Covina and Arcadia. In 1976, he founded Little Caesar Magazine and Press, which he ran until 1982. In 1985, he moved to Amsterdam for two and a half years, where he began his ten year long project, The George Miles Cycle, an interconnected sequence of five novels that includes Closer, Frisk, Try, Guide, and Period. His post-George Miles Cycle novels include My Loose Thread, The Sluts and his most recent novel, the highly acclaimed God, Jr. Other works include the short-story collection Wrong, a collection of poetry titled The Dream Police and All Ears: Cultural Cristicism, Essays and Obituaries. Dennis Cooper currently spends his time between Los Angeles and Paris. His latest work, a limited edition collection of new poems, titled The Weaklings is available now from Fanzine Press.</span>
